#  [](/thread/252157-part-2-eurusd-trend-magic-system)Part 2 EURUSD Trend magic System

  * [#1](/thread/252157-part-2-eurusd-trend-magic-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Aug 23, 2010 1:00am  Aug 23, 2010 1:00am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar56490_3.gif) Paulus](paulus)

  * Joined Dec 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,600 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56490)

**The original thread<http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=165948>**  
**Grew to a size that made it very difficult for new people to gain an insight into the original system.**  
  
**Below is the 1st post on this new thread and will list the original indicators that are used now. Any repainting indictors will not be posted as they created many questions which already in the thread has been answered many times  
  
This system can used on any time frame**  
**I like using it on the 5min and 1min but also have it set up on the daily and hhour I personaly also use it on a daily time frame..**  
  
**I use it primarily on EURUSD this was added 27th July 1020 and hence the change in the Thread title.**  
  
**A few brief lines on the history,**  
  
**I found and used a combination of 2 indicators BB MACD and Trend Magic ( TM).BBMACD was used for gauging of the trend i.e. up or down and the TM was used for entry and stop loss**  
  
**The BBMCD and the TM were then combined into 1 indicator called the HA_0001a this indicator would give a green bar when a BBMACD and TM long signal was present and a red bar when BBMACD and TM sell signal was present**  
  
**This was later developed into the Multy time frame version called HA_0001a_MTF although a good indicator which does not repaint people found it difficult to work with and I will explain why**  
  
**When you have a 5min candle we know the bar opens at 5pm and closes at 5.05pm if we use an MLT indictor that shows 15mins then we have to realise that when the 5min bar closes the 15min bar part of the indicator still has 10 mins to run to complete… hence you get a signal on the 5min you look at the 15min and it confirms the same colour and you take the signal … after 10mins the bar ends on the 15min and its now showing the opposite colour and in hind sight you wouldn’t of taken and perhaps you lose. This caused massive problems when looking back on signals through out the day so although it doesn’t repaint I wont inc it here in this thread  
**  
  
  
**Next post will show indicators and settings**  
  
**  
  
PLEASE KEEP THE THREAD CLEAR OF ALL OTHER INDICATORS ATM**  
  
****  
  
****  
**  
**  
  
****  
**

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar56490_3.gif) Paulus](paulus)

  * Joined Dec 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,600 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56490)

**_SETUP and TRADING  
  
_**  
  
EURUSD as it tends to trend better than most and has a small spread  
  
  
  
Indicators used 4  
  
****Clock_v1_3****  
  
Just gives local time and other broker times plus current candle time  
Tick both boxes under common tab  
Set all to true apart from 12hr time  
  
****Ant-GUBreakout_V.0.4.1****  
  
Place on your chart and play around with the start stop times until the coloured box covers the Asian market in your time Zone.  
  
**_Trend Magic_**  
CCI 50 .. ATR 5  
  
**_BB MACD_ **  
Inputs 144..233..21 on 5 min time frame yep you guessed it Fib numbers  
StDv 1.1  
  
**_Entry long_  
**  
BB MACD blue   
TM goes from red to blue  
  
**_Entry Short_**  
  
BB MACD red   
TM goes from blue to red  
  
**_Exit_**  
  
  
Initial stop hit or sliding stop via TM hit  
  
  
Next post will explain Exit with initial stop placement and sliding SL using TM

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar56490_3.gif) Paulus](paulus)

  * Joined Dec 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,600 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56490)

Details of Stop placement and movement, please read this in conjunction with the chart posted  
  
I will explain in screen shot a b c d etc   
  
A - Signal to go short  
B - Initial stop is 1pip above last swing high ( good technical point for stop)  
From A the TM then slopes down it goes flat and slopes down again when the slope is fixed ..ie cannot move which happens at close of candle C move stop to TM horizontal line at D  
From C the TM goes flat and then moves down when slope is fixed ie.. cannot move which happens at close of candle E move stop to TM horizontal line at F  
  
  
We follow down TM horizontal line with Stop but are ALWAYS 1 level above so we eventualy get stopped out at G for 16 pips  
  
Next post entry conditions

**_From Fridays chart  
_**  
2 entries 1 short 1 long  
  
_**Short**_  
  
Initial BBMACD was red and TM become red from blue on the same bar we have an entry  
  
**_Long_**  
  
Initial BBMACD was blue and TM become blue from red on the same bar we have an entry  
  
If using on the 1min the additional rule is...  
  
When going long close of entry bar must be above TM when going short close of bar must be below TM line

Hey Paul,  
Good to see the new thread without the repainting indicator baggage. Hope it stays this way. I have added a few reminders below, I hope you don't mind me doing this (there is no way to contact you so I could not ask for permission..![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f641.png?v=15.1)).  
  

**SOME INFO FOR NEW PEOPLE**  
  

1\. Make sure you trade while there is enough liquidity. Taking trades in the wee hours of the Tokyo session is not very smart as the system described by Paul can be considered a trend following system. Trading this on an intraday chart requires the right time. Trade with the flow. In the old thread it was suggested to start trading with the London open and I see no reason to deviate from that. Not sure when it opens? See this: <http://www.forexmarkethours.com/markethours.php>  
and this: <http://www.forexmarkethours.com/GMT_hours/02/>  
for the advanced, you might also want to take a look at this, especially if you are considering pairs other than the fiber: <http://www.forexmarkethours.com/volatility/05/>  
  
2\. Please read the whole thread before you start asking questions - some of them have already been answered. As of right now, the thread is only a few posts, which should make it very easy for you. Remember, we are here to make money and you should do your homework before asking for help. However, if you do need help, feel free to ask - there are quite a few people from the old thread who will be willing to help you out.   
  
3\. If you experience any difficulties with your trades, please remember to post a chart with your entry/exit and reasons for entry/exit.  
  
4\. As Paul already said, no additional indicators, please. This is why Paul has resorted to starting a new thread. If you want to know what happened, kindly follow the link of the first post to the previous thread.  
  
Good luck! 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

When it download as *.php then just rename it to what ever the indi is called and put ex4 or mq4 in the end (indiname.ex4).  
Some indicators are compiled and can not be opened by mql editor, only indicator that end with mq4 and be opened with editor.  
  
Hope it helps

  * [#29](/thread/post/3976599#post3976599 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 26, 2010 3:59am  Aug 26, 2010 3:59am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

> [Quoting evynsdad](/thread/post/3976277#post3976277 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Am I reading this correctly?
> 
> Ignored

No.. G is the spot (pun intended) where that particular trade would have been stopped out. The stop is always adjusted to the previous horizontal line, which means that if you are watching a live screen and TM goes flat for some time, you adjust the SL to the previous horizontal line*****. I prefer to use swing highs/lows, but that's just because I've had so much screen time that it has become easy for me.  
  
***** If you are using MT4, always remember to take into account the spread when adjusting SL levels because MT4 displays bid charts. You don't want to get taken out and then watch the price head in the direction of your trade just because you weren't adjusting for spread. 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

I have an indicator that puts an arrow when the MACD crosses its Signal line, but it is MACD only no BB so it may not be useful here.  
  
Also there are several versions of MACDBB. The old thread had the snakelike MACD dots and the BB lines showing. The pictures earlier here didnt.  
I was going to add that if you have the snaklelike dot version, colorchange on the 144-233-21 isnt enough, you need to see the snake move inwards across the Bollinger Band it had been riding or at least straddle it before considering an entry. A little earlier I took a GBPUSD 5 min short trade when the color changed to match TM from a bar or two earlier, but stayed above the upper band and I got stopped out. It was a demo so I dont really care, but looking at other moves I realized it needs to move across the band. I think.

  * [#35](/thread/post/3978137#post3978137 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 26, 2010 5:43pm  Aug 26, 2010 5:43pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

Just a note of caution for anybody who is planning to testdrive or trade (live) this system today or tomorrow on a low timeframe such as M5: the markets are not really in a 'giving' mode right now as they are waiting for figures from the US and UK. Both nations will publish their revised GDP estimates for the second quarter tomorrow. There's been a deluge of bad economic data from the US, but recent high impact news have been unable to rock the boat on either side.   
  
This means that GU, EU and UJ are all moving pretty much sideways until the second estimates of GDP figures have been released. I personally have already reached my weekly goal so I'm keeping out of the market, but if you really feel like you should use every opportunity to test this system, then I suggest to test M1. In current market conditions, with swings between the upper and lower R&S bands, M1 is the only viable TF. So, either wait for normalization or keep out. 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

hi back from hols took an extra week although was at home just opened FF today but have been trading and struggling !  
  
Markets have low volatility Aug always seems to be the same allot of people go away on hols in Aug it must have an impact..looking at friday the TM line was almost flat for 8 hours just immpossible to make money when its like that.  
  
Friday i spent the day scalping with 10pip TP and 10 pip SL on a system I dug out of my bag that uses TM..  
  
If its any good over the coming weeks I will post it on another thread ..  
  
In the mean time lets pray for some volatility because without it the best of systems will just crash and burn  
  
Paulus

This system is really multi faceted and adaptable. I find myself preferring taking trades using 2 other indicators which dont belong being listed here that need to confirm oneanother, but I always leave TM on my charts to help pick out my SL points and sometimes TP levels especially when market entries need an immediate change to the entry to set the initial SL and TP levels and the TM visual makes it quick. It really does help in any number of ways besides trend. I also still usually dont trade against Paulus' longer term setting for the BBMACD and use it to try and stay a little longer regardless of other indicators.

  * [#66](/thread/post/4062699#post4062699 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 1, 2010 4:00am  Oct 1, 2010 4:00am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar50431_6.gif) CanuckCT](canuckct)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Summer is the best time of year! | [1,284 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=50431)

EJ Trade - with the time of day and what was happening with JPY pairs, I was looking for an EJ short and I usually do that time of the evening.  
  
AU Trade - The first sell alert I ignored because I was wanting it to break the nearest low from 2 bars earlier. The next buy signal I ignored because it was below TM. The third signal I took because it was bearish price action re the prior bar and I had a good place to put the stop. And AU had been on a good tear and was pulling back on bigger timeframe. Was also about to break an M5 trendline...I didn't draw the line but I could see it. And overall price action on other USD pairs had some influence. So it was not simply a matter of taking the signal. You can't trade it that way, in my opinion. I treat it as a heads up...and I take it if I like the overall price action and what is happening in general.   
  
I'll post the next trade that doesn't work...not cherry picking the trades.  
  
Cheers  
CanuckCT  
  
  
  
the

> [Quoting simpletrades](/thread/post/4063599#post4063599 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> can someone answer this please.  
>  I'm in Boston--EST. I know London opens 3am EST, but is 2am EST a more general European open or is it premkt London like 8am EST is for NY?
> 
> Ignored

2 AM EST is Frankfurt open (their 9 AM). Some decent volume kicks in around that time. It isn't like 8 AM EST because London/Europe is open (therefore high volume) whereas Frankfurt opens from low volume. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Our 2AM EST is Frankfurt's 8AM and that is when their market opens. Frankfurt is 6 hours ahead and London 5.

I am buy this pair.

I found this thread 2 days ago. Because I don't like second guessing, I read the first instructional post and stopped there. I use my own exit strategy so I didn't need to read any of that. I can say that on Thursday I started trading TM live. First trade lost 8 pips (but that it would seem, is the beauty of this system), trade #2, rode it for 41 pips, then trade number 3 (on Friday) rode it for 86 pips! Closed all trades and banked 119 pips before NFP on Friday (using TM only)! To the man that created these indies (and the template) I say thank you! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44f.png?v=15.1) This system certainly takes K.I.S.S to a new level of Simple!  
  
"Trend Magic"...sort of has a nice ring to it..yes?![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f647-200d-2642-fe0f.png?v=15.1)  
  
Incidentally, if you would like to make it even more powerful, add a few Bill Williams indicators to the chart (Alligator and Fractals). That's just me though, I love Bill Williams System! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35654_2.gif) Vantage](vantage)

  * Joined Mar 2007 | Status: Trader | [7,195 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35654)

> [Quoting TriMagic](/thread/post/4087901#post4087901 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Nice, what time frame is that, M5?
> 
> Ignored

Yes thats 5 min.  
  
Its a clean method of getting in trend. Like anything its not perfect. Take care around certain times and length of run needed to signal a trade eg if its around Frankfurt open (FO) and you've run 30 pips to get a signal, entry there could be a problem. Also take care if the entry candle is too large for the tme frame you are looking at, 15 pips + can be a problem on 5 min. I focus on taking a signal with a lh/hl.  
  
I have used a 1hr 8lwma to approx trend but this does seem a nice alternative.

These are the kind of set ups I'm looking for. No oversize candles nice lower highs or 2 b trades (see right tick price makes a slight high instantly rejected for a shooting star) in line with system. Entry candles have little/no lower wicks.   
  
Pity they were both too early for me. Good examples though.  
  
There is another sell chance below 113.25 but its often a reversal time so we didn't consider.

Sorry for my delayed response. My internet has been un-reliable the last few days. For exiting the trades, I use the flatline of the TM and I move it up as it changes levels. I've gained as many as 86 pips in a single trade or as little as 5 pips. I've lost 3 trades this week for a total for -24 pips, otherwise I am up around 200 pips all together. I have applied the TM to only EUR/USD chart, I monitor the 5M, 1H and daily (do a back test on the daily chart with TM and you'll see what I mean! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f911.png?v=15.1) ) Hope this answers your question!

Right you are. But that is the simplest of exit strategies. I thought you might have been looking for some kind of complicated exit strategy. My philosophy is to keep it simple. Yes, I move the stop up or down as TM changes levels and then wait for the stop to hit! It makes trading fun again! Check the chart I attached today. I took a signal on the hourly chart and was stopped out at 70 pips. I've been using this system for 1 week, and so far can find nothing wrong with it! I've lost count of the pips I've taken, but it's in the 300 to 400 pip range and around an 86% win rate. The bigger winners come from the hourly signals

Hi, just got through the whole thread. Seems a very nice and simple method.  
  
I have question on the entry though:  
  
**_"Entry long  
  
_**BB MACD blue   
TM goes from red to blue  
  
**_Entry Short_**  
  
BB MACD red   
TM goes from blue to red"  
  
1\. As I understand it the BB Macd should already be blue ahead of the TM for long. That is the BB is already blue then the TM turns from red to blue back to color agreement?  
  
2\. Now what if the BB is red, but the TM is blue and I want to look for a long. Do I wait for the BB to go blue, then the TM to go red and change back to blue before entering?   
  
I guess what I'm really asking does the order of the indicators agreeing have to be BB first, and then TM going against and then agreeing?   
  
So, three conditions?:  
  
1\. BB blue or red.  
2\. TM opposite  
3\. TM swithes back to agreement.

  * [#111](/thread/post/4098593#post4098593 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 15, 2010 5:35pm  Oct 15, 2010 5:35pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

> [Quoting KumoDragon](/thread/post/4097368#post4097368 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I guess what I'm really asking does the order of the indicators agreeing have to be BB first, and then TM going against and then agreeing?
> 
> Ignored

Not exactly. According to the original rules, you have to wait for BB to go blue to look for longs. If TM is already blue, you just jump right in. If TM is red, you wait for it to go blue.   
  
I have traded this system quite a lot in terms of screen time and I can tell you that BB is not really that important once you've traded it for a while. The nice thing about this system is that it doesn't really hide the price so once you have enough experience, you are able to use price action and TM only to place your trades. You can and should use BB if you are just starting to use this system, but once you progress, you should be able to see with your own eyes the lower lows, higher highs and so forth. That's what happened to me, anyway. Alternatively, you could place a moving average (some have already done that via CCI, which in essence just shows you whether the price is above or below a certain SMA) to replace BB. I don't want to deviate from Paul's original setup, but I have found the 50 ema very useful when the market is trending. Also, have round numbers marked on your chart before you start trading (a'la 00 and 50 intraday levels).  
  
If you have more questions I'd be glad to answer.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

Hey KD,  
Yep, yep...that'd be Bugs' way, it is worthy to note...  
PA, PA, PA...HL's, LH's...123 pattern, etc.  
Also, note the relationship of EUR/GBP today...Euro is the weaker one,   
so better to look for shorts against USD, YEN, etc.  
Not to mention round numbers as potential targets.  
News is always tough puppy any way, but you did have profit,   
maybe tighten up on the stop to protect profit.  
  
Hope your trades are better for you next week.   
Included a round numbers indy if anyone wants to throw it on their charts.  
  
Cliff

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

> [Quoting KumoDragon](/thread/post/4098999#post4098999 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi, another question.   
>    
>  Here is something that I saw today.  
>    
>  Got up today saw both TM and BB were red. So, I got in short as it didn't look like a bad spot.  
>    
>  Shortly thereafter both BB and TM turned blue, but price had not yet hit my SL.   
>    
>  Instead of waiting for SL I just got out early and took the long.  
>    
>  Is this a good or bad thing to do to use the change of TM/BB as an early exit, before SL?
> 
> Ignored

I'm afraid there aren't any 100% fool-proof rules and you just have to acquire enough screen time to be able to answer those questions. The thing is that I could give you an answer that suits me but I'm not sure it would fit with your trading style (the saying is that each and every one of us has to find a style and a system/strategy that fits their personality). With that mind, however, **_I would like to emphasize that price action can and once you have enough experience, certainly will help you make those calls_**. Vantage has made a very good point in the post that follows your post. Emphasis mine.  
  

> [Quoting Vantage](/thread/post/4099688#post4099688 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I must say having lots of fun on this method, using to trade 5 min higher lows and lower highs. **We do not trade moves through TM even with correct colour changes unless that move itself is a hl/lh**.  
>    
>  Thanks Paulus.
> 
> Ignored

So there you have it. Paul's original system + price action. You could try putting little boxes on an old chart to denote higher highs, lower lows and so on just to get the feel of it. Then proceed to live demo testing and see what you end up with. For me, this seemed a little to much to take in at first but trust me, once you get the feel of it, it will be easier. It will still take all the focus and hard work that you would expect from trading, but the amount of confusion should drop. 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

> Disliked
> 
> Well, tried it today and I lost -151 pips on GU today, over 5 trades, trading the 5M.  
>    
>  Probably not the greatest day to start being friday.  
>    
>  One trade could have been +50 but got stopped out at BE, should have just taken 50 as it was really a news reaction at 7:30.  
>    
>  Looking back my entries could have been better. It seems that the best entry is with the color change, you can't just jump in because the colors agree and hope it continues.  
>

> 
> Ignored

Probably not the greatest day...that's for sure. Now, here's a real shocker for you: you absolutely have to keep an eye on the calendar here at FF and make necessary adjustments to your trading times or lot sizes.   
  
Maybe it's a bit too much to ask, but it would also help your account if you were to check financial news every day to get the big picture (at least once a day, before trading perhaps). You don't have to be a Wall Street analyst to interpret the news that has been hitting financial pages these last few weeks. The big news right now is that Bernanke has been suggesting starting another round of quantitative easing (ie. printing money thereby driving down the dollar). This afternoon Bernanke gave a speech where he touched this matter. About 15 minutes later some important data came out which rocked the USD boat. This is a killer combination of RED impact events all marked in the FF calendar. I'm not mister smartypants so I'm not going to tell you that I knew this was going to happen. But volatility _does pick up_ during these events:  
  
Central banks shape monetary policy  
United States (still) has the largest economy on the planet  
The US dollar is (still) the predominant reserve currency of the world  
**Thus:** anything that the chairman of the Federal Reserve says or does can have a large impact. The same applies for regional Fed presidents, Fed governors, the SOMO chief and a number of vice-chairmen and vice-presidents. This is especially evident in times of change - when economic growth, inflation and/or unemployment stay at a level that is deemed undesirable by the monetary authority.  
  
If this is too much to ask, then trading for profit is perhaps not your thing. Please don't think I'm saying this because I'm trying to outsmart you on a public forum. This is a kill or be killed business and you have to protect your account - reading a bit of financial news and keeping an eye on the FREE calendar at FF is a very simple task and will most likely help you immensely.   
  
When it comes to trading this system, I personally prefer using it with EU rather than GU. GU has higher spread and way lower liquidity. This lower liquidity results in stops being taken out _all of the time_ , which, in chart-speak means that cable doesn't respect S&R levels nearly as much as EU does (GU whips past important S&R levels just to take the stops out and then goes back to where it was). 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#123](/thread/post/4100374#post4100374 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 16, 2010 4:42am  Oct 16, 2010 4:42am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

Coming back to my previous post, here's how I start my day(s):  

  1. I get up. I eat something and make coffee.
  2. I check the news and blogs I follow for important developments.
  3. I check fx talk for overnight developments and order flow.
  4. I write down news release times on a separate sheet I keep by my PC while I trade.
  5. I check high time-frames for R&S.
  6. I check lower TFs for R&S.
  7. I mark off round numbers (you could do this with an indicator).
  8. I start trading with minimal size.
  9. If I feel everything is going alright, I switch to bigger lot sizes. If I don't feel confident enough or something is bugging me OR there is a huge red impact news coming, I wait.
  10. Once I have reached my daily goal, I pretty much quit trading for the day (not always). Some people don't operate with daily goals in mind because they feel it puts too much pressure on them. I feel that this is a personal choice type of issue (kind of like whether you prefer higher or lower TFs).

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

  * [ KumoDragon](kumodragon)

Here are my stupid stupid trades from friday, Oct. 16th. Any comments of how I could have done better, using this threads method, are welcome.  
  
Trade are marked with a green or red dot for long or short. The trades are all taken on the 5M on GU. I only trade GU.  
  
My breakout box is set to 11:00 -13:00  
  
1\. Short loss: Had just got up TM and BB were red and price was close to it, so I got in short. Almost as soon as I got in both turned blue so I got out.  
  
2\. Long BE: Got in right after both tm and bb turned blue. Waited for the news. Could have taken +50 but instead I put trade at BE and was stopped out.  
  
3\. Long loss: The hammer before my entry made it look like it was just a higher low to me, so I got back in after my stop out at BE. It of course then tottally reversed.  
  
4\. short loss: TM & BB turned red and had a big candle going through TM. Price of course then reversed on me then TM and BB turned blue so I got out  
  
5\. Long Loss: Because of TM and BB turning blue I got in long again, and of course price reversed on me again and BB and TM turn red. This time I just wait for my stop and am stopped.  
  
6\. Short Loss: Got in after I was stopped out thinking that since everything is the right color for short it will continue and since price made it a point to go so far to stop me out. But, no I picked a bottom again and price reverses. I get out in disgust and quit for the day. And of course if I'd held on this one could have been a winnner.  
  
P.S. Please note that everytime the TM had a color change so did the BB, which is why I asked what is even the point of the using the BB, or is there a better way to use it.

> Ignored

It seems to me that you exit your potentially winning trades with a loss, instead of being patient.   
Use hard stop that is initially under/above last low/high. If it is too far away then better do not take the trade but wait for the next opportunity.  
Anyway, do not jump out only because the line changes color. Supertrend (TM) is tradeable even without paying any attention to its color. Just above or under is the information you need, and the break of the line is the strongest signal.

  * [#135](/thread/post/4101037#post4101037 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 17, 2010 2:12am  Oct 17, 2010 2:12am 

  * [ Indrek](indrek)

  * Joined Jun 2009 | Status: Trader | [2,430 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=106754)

> [Quoting kedridder](/thread/post/4101024#post4101024 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Indrek,  
>  First of all, thank you for contributing to the thread. It seems he did the right thing. While the BB MACD switches direction, he changes along too. Any reason why you said he's being impatient? Perhaps you can share with us?
> 
> Ignored

I just suggest to use hard stop instead of manual exits based on instincts. Any indicator can change its color back and forth, we have to trust our entries.  
Of course, the first thing is to pick the correct entries. In this case, there were false entries, too. But at least two short ones would be winners if the trader did not exit too early.  
Again: initial SL (hard stop) is under/above last low/high. Another option with this system is the previous flat level of TM. If these are too far away - no trade.   
I do not take trades from M5 timeframe if the SL would be more than 25-30 pips.

>  Again: initial SL (hard stop) is under/above last low/high. Another option with this system is the previous flat level of TM. If these are too far away - no trade.

> 
> Ignored

  
i see. thank you! this clears up my noobish mind. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

> [Quoting KumoDragon](/thread/post/4101075#post4101075 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Though I tend to like GU better as it has bigger moves when it takes off.  
>    
>  Do you trade EU during the US session?  
>    
>  P.S. mmmmm looking back the same friday I got boned in GU, EU would have had a great day with this method compared to GU.
> 
> Ignored

Pardon my language, but that's a really uneducated approach. You could just as well trade fiber with bigger lots to compensate for the smaller pip runs. Cable is like an untrained horse, as it were - it runs as fast as hell but it knocks you off if you don't know what you're doing. Fiber is a much more tame animal - it moves slower and the moves are in clear bounds, making it psychologically and monetarily easier to stay on the saddle. All of this goes back to what I wrote earlier about the liquidity of those two pairs. So, if you want to make more money, why don't you consider trading fiber with lots sizes big enough to compensate for the opportunity cost of cable's appealing pip runs?  
  
I do trade the US session but not as often as I used to. Since I live in Europe, I find it most convenient to trade the European open and late morning session. A few days a week I might trade the EU-US overlap session, but that depends on the amount of macro work I have on hand at any specific time. To be honest, I'm not a big fan of the US session as I tend to have difficulties understanding the way price behaves on a minute by minute basis during that time. I still trade it, but with more care. 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

  * [#148](/thread/post/4101510#post4101510 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 17, 2010 4:30pm  Oct 17, 2010 4:30pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35654_2.gif) Vantage](vantage)

  * Joined Mar 2007 | Status: Trader | [7,195 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35654)

> [Quoting KumoDragon](/thread/post/4100948#post4100948 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I'm familiar with looking for H/L/H sequence through using sonic. ( Stopped using that because there were some good trade because of it, but also a lot of fakeouts)  
>    
>  My questions would be when do you enter using trendmagic and H/L/H, do you wait for it to pass to the other side of TM or just when it looks like a continuation from a lower high (short) or higher low (long).  
>    
>  Also when it hits the lower high, how do you know its not just going to continue upward? Or are you just using the direction of the TM + the higher low as your bias?
> 
> Ignored

I don't want this thread to become a hl/lh thread when there are several (including mine) but very briefly: FO/LO each are likely to have reversals around half an hour in, 7.30 gmt and 8.30 gmt. I look to trade hl/lh's and 2b trades in that time frame exactly as per my thread. Once LO range has been broken hopefully the LO head fake has played its hand and the session range will follow. From there its follow TM as per Paulus with hl/lh's. If 8-10 gmt is quiet then you guessed it the move is likely to happen around 11-1pm gmt. If London range decent then around 11-1 gmt it might well consolidate around its extremes waiting for early US to chip in.  
  
Does this happen every day, of course not, does it happen often enough to build a method around (like Paulus' here) yes. So you can take something like this and some knowledge of likely times of moves in the market and build a method. Always remembering that if you have entered on right side of trend and you've had a test of direction (a hl/lh) and trend resumes again the odds are put that little bit better in your favour.  
  
So we are looking for hl/lh's on the correct side of TM, if the hl/lh occurs on a TM cross thats also fine, but make no mistake we're looking for hl/lh's ie the test and confirmation of trend.   
  
Hope this helps, if unclear perhaps discussion better served on a hl/lh thread and keeping this for TM trades.

Hi Kumo  
Your trades:  
1) Its definitely a lh but price doesn't go 1 pip below the candle. That alone would have failed my final requirement. This little trick will save you some losing trades, honest.  
3) In and around news will do that at times. Nothing you can do.  
4 and 5) Price action has moved much too far to get in, on the sell that last large candle is from 6061 to 6025, much to big and increases your stop and risk level much too much. I get worried at 15+ pip candles.  
6) Again a very large candle closing on RN, both very dangerous. Price doesn't go 1 pip lower below 1.60 but the size of candle, RN both would have kept me out.  
  
Hope this helps a little.

I just eyeball.  
  
Same eur chart, left arrow, clear lh but TM hasn't turned around yet.  
  
2nd from left. There is a lh close on 4075, that prob would be a losing entry with a small stop. Price then tries for 1.41 fails for a nice lh trade below the RN. So if you count this as a -12 ish and a + whatever but bigger than 12.  
  
3rd arrow from left, I definitely would not have let this go to a losing trade from prob close to +20 up.  
  
The x has now made a higher high from prev trade so its a difficult sell to make.  
  
Right arrow down another lh that works nicely but perhaps late in session.  
  
All the sells have nice lh's, entry candles have little/small lower wicks, none of set up candles are overly large.  
  
You decide on your own stop, take profit levels, or whether you'll follow system. Entry 1 pip or so below the set up candle you identify as the lh.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar51108_2.gif) Colostarr](colostarr)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Oct 2007 | [1,015 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=51108)

> [Quoting kedridder](/thread/post/4103416#post4103416 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Thats very good! cool 50 PIPS there.   
>  For your own strategy, does the BB MACD play a part here?
> 
> Ignored

Rarely...from my experience in this forum, people try to learn a new system and stick to it to the very letter. Which is good, but use judgement. I love to set and forget, and I take the greed factor OUT of my exit strategy. If I see a setup, I take it, if the pair SPIKES (actually took a 100 pip bearish move on Friday!), I close the trade and put the pips in my bank. If it trends in a favorable direction, I move the stops in accordance with the entry instructions, if the stop hits, it hits, if not not I keep moving it until it does get hit. The system is so simple, it is designed to minimize your losses and maximize your profits. If you get a signal, take it, if it spikes close it, if not move your stops until you get stopped out (K.I.S.S). Be happy with the PIPS you get, but you must also be happy with the PIPS you lose. To answer your question, I use the BB MACD for entry (per the instructions), I use my head for the exit. I've lost 2 trades (-8 pips) last week, I banked well over 400 exiting when it felt good using TM for entry. I took one trade today +12 pips, which takes me to 11 consecutive wins using TM since Monday last. Choose your entries carefully, and NEVER give back pips TAKE THEM!. This is strictly my method and in no way am I trying to circumvent the creators strategies. Trend Magic is a phenomenal system! I've been trading live for 5 years now, this is by far the easiest and most profitable system I've seen in those five years! Just keep it Simple!

Sure thing...attached is an hourly EUR/USD from Friday. I took the short signal from the very large inverted hammer (note TM is blue). The TM turned red afterwards (when it changed it only served to tell me to stay in the trade). I set the short at 1.40736, my first stop was set at 1.40171 (actually the FIRST stop was at the high of the previous candle) and again at 1.39210. I stepped away from my computer for a few hours, when I returned the EUR/USD had just formed a bullish inverted candle (very nice one). The decision was too easy, I didn't use TM's exit strategy (that would have cost me around 45 pips!), I set my stop at the high of the bullish candle and within 15 minutes the stop hit and I banked 202 pips! I hope this helps!

Normally I trade the 5 minute. This particular day the news that hit caused volatile movement. The 5M chart became too erratic to attempt a trade, so I switched to the hourly. At that point I was not concerned with TM, the very large bearish candle SCREAMED short entry (get a copy of Bill Williams book trading Chaos 2nd edition). The angulation formed from the alligators mouth had my mouth watering! Again the TM had NOT given a short signal, the hammer and alligator did! The TM changed color later and made me feel better about riding the wave and staying in the trade...I'm glad I did it was a good day! Most of the trades I make with TM are from the 5M chart though, you can scalp the crap even out of a ranging market! It's phenomenal! If you get a chance take a look at the Daily chart on the EUR/USD with a TM template...I am still waiting for a color change on that..VERY POWERFUL!![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f911.png?v=15.1)

My 2cents. Try this on higher timeframes and you can cut out all the noise such as economic news. However your money management and your account size should permit that.

  * [#173](/thread/post/4105617#post4105617 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 19, 2010 2:00pm  Oct 19, 2010 2:00pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar51108_2.gif) Colostarr](colostarr)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Oct 2007 | [1,015 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=51108)

I haven't had ANY re-painting issues, nor will I try to find any. Doing this creates doubt in the traders mind, and makes you second guess an entry! The TM is a moving average, and to my knowledge it WILL repaint while that candle is active. I have yet to see TM repaint a closed candle. While TM is a great system, there are other basic trading principles that everyone should ALWAYS apply, News, daily and weekly pivot points, hammers, inverted hammers, double tops, bear or Bull traps the list is endless. Don't become a slave to just ONE system. I found that TM augments other systems very nicely (as an example Bill Williams method "Trading Chaos", there is a thread in this forum that covers this method). Just don't loose sight or get "tunnel vision" for just one method! Be a smart trader and stick to basics first! Don't make a system harder than it needs to be. Just my 2 cents!![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f914.png?v=15.1)

  * [#174](/thread/post/4105632#post4105632 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:13pm  Oct 19, 2010 2:10pm | Edited 2:13pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar51108_2.gif) Colostarr](colostarr)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Oct 2007 | [1,015 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=51108)

That was a BEAUTIFUL signal! You ignored it because you didn't stick to the systems most basic entry rule, when TM and BB change color at the same time it's an ENTRY. Because of that very basic and simple fact, I would have MOST definitely taken that signal! Who cares what time of day it was ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f633.png?v=15.1)? You need to keep it simple, TAKE AN ENTRY SIGNAL, set your stop loss and wait (PATIENCE!). As a general rule I almost always set a limit or stop 5 to 10 pips beyond my stop loss price. If the market is trending you'll make good on the signal, if it is ranging, hopefully you can recover your losses and then some. For future reference when TM gives you a signal TAKE IT! Hope this helps!  
  
Edit: it looks to me from your chart that you ignored roughly a 60 pip move...knowing what you know now, would you have taken that signal ?  
  

> [Quoting KumoDragon](/thread/post/4104946#post4104946 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> As per the TM and BB there was a potential short on the EU at 20:30, which is 3:30 in the afternoon here.  
>    
>  I saw it but ignored it because of the time of day.  
>    
>  Would anyone else who is trading this method have taken it, and why?
> 
> Ignored

Yes it does. And what feels better is that I didn't spaz out and do 5 trades within one session trying to find the best direction of the morning to be in.  
  
Just thought I'd upload a jpeg of todays trade so anyone who is interested or has comments, observations, tips, and or questions could see.  
  
I got in a bit later then I would have liked. Got out of bed at 6 Am and was still rubbing my eyes when my screens came on and price was jumping around in that little range there. Had I been up a bit before 6 Am I could have caught a better entry.  
  
Anyway, everything lined up to my eyes good enough so I got in with a stop behind the last lower high and just kept moving my SL down with TM.  
  
I put my SL early to +60 thinking it would reverse. I should have just left my initial TP which was +100 and hit before the move past that stop level. Can't complain though +60 is really nice.

Ya, one of the things that attracted me to this thread was trend following AND trailing stop set up of TM.  
  
Of the methods I've been toying with the past few months from FF none have had a dicernable, repeatable, and logical way to trail and lock profit that doesn't always take you out too early and give you room to follow more potential move, while still at least locking in decent profit. Trend magic seems to adress that nicely  
  
What I'm really looking for is a way to get up at 6 AM and determine what will be the most dominant direction or trend of the day and stay in as long as I can. Try to catch as much of the move between 6 Am & 11\. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Aren't we all? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
What I do is keep an eye on the news. Sometimes it gives you a heads up, sometimes it doesn't. Right now, however, there is a lot of talk about BOE doing more QE (thus the cable weakness today). The Chinese surprise interest rate hike took a bit of steam off risk assets (thus the fiber, gold & other risky asset selloffs). It takes a bit of time to do this and to guesstimate the eventual impact of those stories, but I might say that if you want to stick to trading for the long run, it will certainly not do you any harm to follow the news. Not religiously, having a general grasp of things is good enough.  
  
Analyzing longer term charts is another way of doing it, although this too isn't perfect (nothing is). Right now it looks like the dollar is headed for a rebound (if you're trading dollar pairs, have a look at USDX), at least in the very near term (some of it has already fed through). There might be some more dollar weakness going forward, but that will be decide by the FOMC meeting on November 3rd.  
  
I've already taken up quite a bit of space so I'm going to stop here. Don't want to lead the thread too far off the main topic. 

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

  * [#203](/thread/post/4111764#post4111764 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:19pm  Oct 21, 2010 10:53am | Edited 2:19pm 

  * [ KumoDragon](kumodragon)

  * | Joined Sep 2009  | Status: Trader | [1,048 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=116472)

Here is a jpeg of my last two winnning trades using trend magic.  
  
The first was my long I already posted about earlier +89 from the US session.  
  
The second was a short. I followed trend magic rules for entry but put a wider stop (60 pips) , above a resistance that rejeceted price strongly on the 4 H in the past. Normally I wouldn't have a stop this wide using trend magic.   
  
However, because of the huge long spike in the US session and the consolodation that followed, I expected that there would be a reversal short, if nothing else for profit taking from big dog trader. And that if it didn't go my way after consolodation perhaps the resistance above might reject price.  
  
The thick blue lines show entry and exit Long, and red for the short.  
  
I also did not follow the TM rules for exiting on the short. The short movement was so swift that I just locked in 50 with a postive SL, I've seen spikes that fast reverse hard too often.  
  
P.S. Pair is the EU, it's the only one I trade at the moment, and it's as crazy as hell this week.

> [Quoting david4u](/thread/post/4112489#post4112489 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Comments are welcome
> 
> Ignored

Then that's what you're going to get. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
I hope you can still see the price behind what I drew on your chart. I've been banging on about higher/lower lows and highs in a couple of my posts. Now I get to show what I mean. Now, what I'm about to tell you is not that easy to follow through when you're actually trading, but I hope this will help you see what I deem a good entry point considering higher lows and all that stuff.   
  
On your chart, your entry was at point C. You have already marked two higher lows on your chart that preceded your entry. However, points B and A would have provided a better entry point. Point X marks the spot where you had your first HL. This tells you that something is about to change, since price bottomed at a higher point that before.   
  
The way I see it, you have two potential entry points:  
1\. Reference point A. Once price has already made a higher low, you enter when price breaks through the high that it reached before making the HL.  
  
2\. A higher probability trade could have been taken at reference point B. First you waited for price to make a higher low at point X. Then you wait for it to blast through the high at point A. You enter once price breaks through the last reference high at point B. This is the highest high we've had since price made a higher low and this is a very good entry point.   
  
[There is a third possibility. You wait for the price to blast through point B, make a higher low and then enter once it starts going up again.]  
  
If I have confused you then let me know. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

Name: fiber 7 CRB.png

people somehow use it to trade with some kind of breakout.  
i only use it to color in blue the times of day for a given pair i dont want to be entering a trade and color the silver lines black to get rid of them.  
i set the start and stop to coincide with chart times of when i no longer want to be entering and it stops blue when i want to be watching.  
too easy to overtrade just because tm recolors with bbmacd at the wrong session.

G-Man  
I am trying to combine Vantage's HL/LH as I understand it with the TM sys. In other words , If I get a signal , eg  
Blue TM +Blue BBMACD , I will to enter the trade unless I see that price have made HL/LH.  
In my chart you can see that I have entered close to the HL , so it was not a classic break out of the 123 pattern ,  
but I may enter on BO's also.  
Hope it help  
David

  * Nov 11, 2010 8:09am  Nov 11, 2010 8:09am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar129856_14.gif) bug](bug)

  * Joined Jan 2010 | Status: cash is a position too | [958 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=129856)

Attention!   
Anyone that uses the ant-gu breakout box to mark the Asian session (or any other session) should make necessary changes due to shifts in daylight savings time. From November 1st London time = Greenwich Mean Time (GMT). This stems from the fact that London adjusts the clock but GMT is fixed (during the summer, London time = GMT+1. If you are trading the Frankfurt session, please note that Germany adjusted their time as well. More information is available here: <http://www.timeanddate.com/time/dst/2010.html>  
and here: <http://www.forexmarkethours.com/>

If you don't risk, you don't ever have to lose.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

This is one of the best indi based systems around that I've seen. You cannot however take every cross and expect to be OK, that won't happen. With respect take this method but have a look at (shameless plug but it may help) my higher low lower high thread. Take this concept with higher lows and lower highs and it honestly should help some. Also be careful of the size of the run taken to generate a signal, times of day (London open head fake to name just one) and the size of the candle that generated the signal to name just a few of the other items to be considered.  
  
Post your trades with charts and let people discuss, you'll learn more from your losing trades than your winners.

  * Nov 20, 2010 7:05pm  Nov 20, 2010 7:05pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar52245_6.gif) Evaluator](evaluator)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,972 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=52245)

Is is possible to take the **BB_MACD_CCT_alerts_v2** indicator and turn it into an EA for any currency pair and in any time period? Where Buy and Sell is executed on the close of the candlestick? or has someone already made this into an EA?  
  
Can someone point me in the right direction? i would like to back test this as an ea. Here would be the specs  
  
1\. The EA initiate a buy or sell based on the color of the candlestick red= sell and blue = buy.  
  
2\. Once an order is in place the ea would not initiate another order until a change in the candlestick color or the user places a stop loss on the order ( a parameter default is none but the user can change in the settings )  
  
3\. The user would need to be able to adjust the following settings:  
Fast Len default is 144  
Slow Len default is 233  
Length default is 21  
StDiv default is 1.1  
UseAlert default is true  
  
Lot Size default is 0.1  
Stop Loss default is none   
Order Initiation default is candlestick close  
  
Basically, it is taking the BB_MACD_CCT_alerts_v2 indicator and adding the last 3 values and making it an EA and not a indicator.  
  
This has exciting possibilities!  
  
Please point me in the right direction.  
  
Thanks.[http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/s...im/winking.gif](http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/smilies/yim/winking.gif)  
  
(_Indicator is attached for all you programmers out there_)

  * [#237](/thread/post/4187053#post4187053 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 21, 2010 9:46am  Nov 21, 2010 9:46am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar52245_6.gif) Evaluator](evaluator)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,972 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=52245)

Okay, fine. I know programming is not easy, I have tried it but have been unsuccessful. I know that writing the code for the indicator was not easy either but someone did it and gave it away freely. I know that comming up with this system was definitely not easy but someone did it. (THANK YOU PAULUS!)  
  
I too have tested this system for atleast 40 man hours and have been experimenting with different timeframes.   
  
I do have issues with the system.  
  
1\. repaints. the trend majic indicator repaint alot in the lower time frames (especially 5 min.) that causes miss calls and throws the entire systems reliability in jepardy.  
  
2\. whipsaws. the BB MACD also whipsaws a great deal making it difficult to determine the best/optimal point of entry for an order.  
  
3\. currency pairs. the eurusd seems to be one of the worst pairs to use this system in the 5 and 15 min timeframes. 30 min seems to be more stable but as you get to 4 hr and daily the TM becomes unstable again. Has anyone used other currency pairs and found them reliable with TM?  
  
4\. timespan. Since the market runs solid from Sunday evening until Friday night and the market activity periods are set at different times of the day London, NY, Tokyo, it is physically impossible for a person to remain awake at all times and if they do it is not healthy. My only reason for suggesting an EA is because it can function 24hours a day and we would then have something we could back test. I am not saying this is the answer. Actually, this would provide the basics to better evaluate and fine tune the system.   
  
Also, your speech about others willingness of others to program for the group is incorrect. I have seen and have worked with people trying to perfect a system by making it into an EA. Some people are willing to give it a go for the sake of proving a system after all, people took the time to create the indicators and then modify and post it for the group for free. So, you are wrong with your statements.   
  
Lastly, "bug" dear responder, please let us work together and not be so negative. I am trying to look at this in an objective positive manner. Are you?  
  
I would not ask questions if I did not think this system had value. In fact I think this is a great concept and the system has great potential.   
  
I would not bother to spend a week testing the system if I did not think it had merit. So, please stop with all the spattering about my request and questions.  
  
Can't we be friends and get along?![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
  
P.S. Let us take this offline out of this thread. If you wish to discuss further and make comments let us do that beweeen us. I wish to concentrate on the Trend Majic system than argue.

Well...  
I would disagree, myself, that the TM repaints on any TF....those bugs were worked out long ago...when the candle closes on any TF, it does not change color...it's a non-issue.  
The MACD does not whip saw if the 144, 233, 21 default Fib. numbers are used...very smooth in transition when moving in Trend.  
I would even go so far as to say that an EA will never be made for this method as it's variables are way to complex to program successfully. Sure it would be nice, but it ain't happenin'.  
As far as times to trade, London, New York, Asia, etc., well, pick your poison...  
If the market is trending then look for some entries...if it's not, then go do something else with your time...  
After all, the thread is about an indicator called... Trend Magic  
  
Let us here no further talk of this EA business...  
  
Enjoy the weekend, Trading Bro...  
  
Cliff

I do not know about the indicator that some people call TrendMagic - if it repaints or not. What I know is that the indicator's other and best known name is Supertrend and it does not repaint. I have posted it many, many times in FF, and people still use wrong versions with bugs...  
I am a heavy user of Supertrend. All systems that I use, include it as one of the main elements.   
What I can say in connection with Paulus' system is that:  
1) it is one of the best that I have found in FF;  
2) if a trader has little understanding about the market then it may demand at least some other filter(s);  
3) if a trader has absolutely no understanding about the market then it is better for him to find another hobby;  
4) the system works best for EU and EY, especially EU.

You should learn to trade first and then start talking about an EA. In any case, singling out last Friday as a bad day for trading just goes to prove show that you can't trade thus making your suggestions for a possible EA quite useless, really. You will find a chart with possibles entries attached. But let's step back for a minute - even if Friday were a losing day, it would not matter as the system has proven itself over and over again. If you want to use it to its fullest potential, you first have to learn it. If everyone else has put in the time and effort to learn how to trade and learn how to use this system, why do you expect a fast road to riches with a 'simple' EA?

This is one of the easiest systems to trade. If you focus on trading when the trend is changing and not try to trade every time price crosses TM, it is profitable. And you can trade the cross of TM in the direction of the prevailing trend with a little price action. With good money management, you should be able to handle the losing trades. I don't see what there is to bicker about on a simple system like this.   
  
Friday EURUSD

The very first post says it very concisely...  
  
**"I found and used a combination of 2 indicators BB MACD and Trend Magic ( TM).BBMACD was used for gauging of the trend i.e. up or down and the TM was used for entry and stop loss"  
  
**It's not any more complicated than this.   
  
It might be productive to post some trades in real time....and folks could comment. This approach works on other pairs and other timeframes....  
  
Cheers  
CanuckCT

It is a very simple and effective system. As indicator systems go this is less stressful than most as it provides entries and exits mechanically. I will only use the three inidicators ie price action, supertrend and bb macd combinded with my s/r levels. They all fit very nicely.

cce   
  
thanks for the feedback. i would not use it in 5 min. i would recommend 30 min or 1 hr timeframe because it will clear up alot of the whipsaw acton that occurs to frequently in especially from what I have seen in the BB MACD indicator and the repaints in the trend majic.  
  
i like the use of BB MACD and trend majic indicator. i am always looking for indicators that can identify the true top and bottoms of a major wave movement. that is why i find these indicators so useful.   
  
i just downloaded supertrend and will test this week to see how well it acts with repaints. hopefully it will removes the repaint issue with the trend majic indicator repain problem.  
  
the 3 level zz semafor indicator is good for identifing the exhaustion areas of ups and downs. on major movements you can make good returns. the problem i have is that sometimes it will identify a top as a strong 3 when it is actually a 2 so you have to watch it.   
  
again i would not use 3 level zz semafor indicator on 5 min charts because of the whipsaw actions that can stop you out.  
  
good luck trading.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)

Then use the Supertrend (another name for TM) indicator that Indrek has posted.

bug,  
  
yes, you are belittling but i can see that is your nature. the difference between us is i am a strategic trader and you are a tactical trader so we are destine to look at things from different perspectives and see things completly opposite....![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f620.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f94a.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f620.png?v=15.1)  
  
i recognize that even though you may not.   
  
therefore, i understand why elliott waves will be completely alien to your trading habits. elliott waves are are used more for strategic trading by identifing trends and the wave structures they contain.   
  
i will admit that i am looking for longer trades that can get me 100s of pips per trade and not 5 pips here and 9 pips there because unless you are trading huge lots (very risky) because the returns are justified for 5 pip trades when you look at the amount of effort, time, and stress to make those trades.  
  
don't misunderstand i like these indicators because they have the potential to find exhaustion points in major drives. paulus has done a good job by putting it out there for us to see and i thank him for his kindness.  
  
also, you are correct i like trading in longer tf because they tend to be more stable. i find that with these indicators 15min, 30 min, and 1 hr tend to better.

  * [#269](/thread/post/4190068#post4190068 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 11:55pm  Nov 22, 2010 11:43pm | Edited 11:55pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35654_2.gif) Vantage](vantage)

  * Joined Mar 2007 | Status: Trader | [7,195 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35654)

You can get in with small stops meaning runs like this give ROI of around 5-7% from 1% risk. You only need to get a couple of these a month with smaller trades here and there to have a great return.  
  
For me the left arrow would have been a stretch due to sideways pa and 15 min was indecisive, 2nd arrow from left would have been an entry for me (no trades at all today due to some major thunder storms computer was off).  
  
Eur and gu basically the same pic as this.  
  
Avoid sideways pa, avoid 40-50 pip runs that generate 1st signal, avoid entry candles that are overly large. Lower highs/higher lows along the way can get you in if first trade missed. My 2c.

Hi guys,  
  
I have been using the following indicators in my account with great success.  
  
1) Supertrend nrp.  
2) BB MACD  
3) Nonlag lot.  
4) 3_level_semafor  
  
I use 15 min char for entry. Look at supertrend and nonlag dot.  
  
BBMACD is slightly lagging compared to Nonlagdot.  
  
The exit has been my problem. I come out too early if i use my money management rules ( 1:1). If i use any of the indicators above for exit, i feel i loose some pips.  
  
What is best strategy for exit?  
  
Thanks to all the wonderful indicators.

It was mentioned in an earlier post that yesterday was a good trading opportunity to make money, but it is not always like that as you know. However, it is still not difficult to make pips every day using this system even when the market is slow. The supertrend and the bb indicator are very good even when the market is tight (ie to keep you out as well as in the trade).  
  
Simplicity is key which is what this system is:-)

50 pips today, yesterdays big fall and easy trades I missed due to storms here. So yes can easily believe 128 pips. Low stress, small stops, generally low draw down before trades move on.  
  
For newer traders compare the above ej, eur charts posted to this go nowhere junk on gu. Look at the last gu move that generated the single red dot. Took 40 pips move to generate that signal. The entry candle alone was around 17 pips, not the kind of set up that will generate low risk trades.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> ...interested to see if PA is signalling short ahead of the indies on EU atm. By definition i guess it should do, but the indie lag sometimes saves us from poorer trades, we'll see.  
>    
>  Edit: updated chart attached, TM flirted with a short signal but BB still firmly long.
> 
> Ignored

This is a wrong entry based on PA.   
  
I would simply follow the Trend indicator and enter long or short. It is a lagging indicator but as you said it avoids you from wrong entry.  
  
See what happened today. If you have followed trend indicator, you may not have entered short at 1.3320. !  
  
Indicator is great and if we follow that strictly, it is still great !  
  
By following a lagging indicator, you are on 'Track" even if you are not catching the "top" or "bottom" 

Intraday only.

  * [#326](/thread/post/4203582#post4203582 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 28, 2010 7:05pm  Nov 28, 2010 7:05pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar52245_6.gif) Evaluator](evaluator)

  * Joined Oct 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,972 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=52245)

Can someone explain their exit strategy.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f615.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/2753.png?v=15.1)   
  
When should one exit a trade;(4 examples)  
  
1\. When the color of one of the two indicators change?   
  
_Opinion:This tends to lead to premature exit of a trend._  
  
2\. When the color on both the indicators change?   
  
_Opinion: This tends to give up a significate amount of profit on some trades and make profitable trades a loss on other occurances._  
  
3\. When you have candles setting higher highs on the sell or lower lows on a buy?  
  
_Opinion:This also can lead to premature exit of a trend and loss of greater profit.(sometimes sigfnificant profit)_  
  
4\. When the trendline in broken on a direction?  
  
_Opinion:This is the old school way for me as I am a trend trader. However, it does have its downside especially when working in a 5min environment because it can get you out of a trade with no profit or even small loss.  
  
_I have played with it in those 4 scenarios. How does the group exit a trade?  
  
Also, do you use a stop loss? If so, what level? I use 100 pips.  
  
Lastly, the Supertrend indicator seems to be more stable than the original indicator listed in this tread. Supertrend does not repaint like the other and therefore is more constant.  
  
Thanks in advance for your input.![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [ Dave1](dave1)

I like to enter a trade when supertrend has 'turned the corner' so to speak, indicating trend direction. Observing the above posts and my own charts when supertrend is flat that to me indicates indecision and a ranging market.

Hi canuc, sorry i did not reply to you but game has replied.  
  
I have been using non lag dot indicator and supertrend very successfully.  
  
I enter long once i see non lag dot changing colour from red to blue. Take profit 10 pips stop loss previous swing low. Almost 10 pips stop loss. It works perfect.Vice versa for short.  
  
But as this author of thread has said, when trend magic line is showing "long" and non lag dot shows blue, you can take more pips, not 10 pips. Just try it out. all the best. 

Intraday only.

Don't expect this to be any better than what you have here <http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=214635> this is a method like any other and blindly entering when 2 things happen won't help. It still (and always will) be trading price action, candles etc etc. These indis are just trying to keep you on the right side of short term trend.  
  
TM/supertrend is basically trading right side of CCI 50 (Steve Hopwoods thread explains).   
  
I don't know what nonlag dot is but you could just as easily chuck on an 8 lwma on your charts, they're so close.   
  
All of a sudden trading above below CCI levels with an 8 lwma doesn't sound so special. That basically is what the Andrew thread is. If it works for you fine, good luck.

Hi all,  
  
I took the liberty of modifying the last version of the STnrp by using the output of the CyclePeriod indie (from Ehlers' book) as the internal CCI period (instead of the fixed 50 period).   
  
You need both attachments in the indicators folder, but put only Adaptive SuperTrend on the chart, insted of TM or current ST, if you want to play with it.   
  
The variations are minor at a glance, but might prove useful, depending on one's entry style I guess ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1). 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [Adaptive SuperTrend.mq4](/attachment/file/594071?d=1291743576) 7 KB | 1,599 downloads 

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [CyclePeriod.mq4](/attachment/file/594072?d=1291743576) 4 KB | 1,266 downloads

>  You need both attachments in the indicators folder, but put only Adaptive SuperTrend on the chart, insted of TM or current ST, if you want to play with it.

> 
> Disliked

> 2 trades this am. +12 +25.

> Ignored

i saw that first entry opportunity but was trying to figure out the importance of EURUSD and EURGBP to a successful GBPUSD move.  
EURUSD was climbing back but its TM and BBMACD were short so that concerned me and EURGBP was confirming short --which made sense since the GBP relative to the EUR was therefore climbing, but 2 bars later EURGBP reversed direction although its TM BBMACD didnt.  
  
I kind of thought EURGBP at that time of day was more controlling on the GBP than EURUSD would be on the USD since US markets and banks were closed. But I still passed on the long entry. Is there a co-dependence? I see a lot that EURUSD and EURGBP need to be moving the same direction for an entry of either to work irregardless of whether both TM BBMACDs are the same color for the 2 symbols.

  * Jan 22, 2011 6:42pm  Jan 22, 2011 6:42pm

>  EURUSD was climbing back but its TM and BBMACD were short so that concerned me and EURGBP was confirming short --which made sense since the GBP relative to the EUR was therefore climbing, but 2 bars later EURGBP reversed direction although its TM BBMACD didnt.

> 
> Ignored

I don't watch eurgbp at all so cannot comment there. I used to have swissy up to check that all are agreeing. 1 has to lead generally so if you miss that one then may get chance to trade the other that catches up. I have taken swissy off.  
  
Am looking to concerntrate on trading in line with daily and viewing anything else as counter trend.  
  
Cannot remember which trader said it but 'if its going up buy it, if its going down sell it'. So if daily is up I'm happier buying etc etc.  
  
So daily was up, we had broken above a D res area, 5900 from 14 Dec, and the Asian move down was rejected on 1hr. So quite happy to buy retraces on something going up.  
  
On eu (as mentioned on hl/lh thread) I was expecting problems 3500-3550 so I just decided to leave that one and focus on gu. If I was watching Fri pm here (US open) a perfect upper close little upper wick hammer on 1hr would have given confidence I think to buy. It closed on 3550 area and one of my other rules of thumb is smaller bounces from key areas = good chance of fail of that key level. You'll see from 5 min the hl's going into US open suggested level would fail and move up had good chance.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar105831_3.gif) Jani72](jani72)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [40 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=105831)

.. if you are interested in BB-MACD I suggest you read and learn how to use it! In my opinion and experience just looking at BB-MACD color is not much more than looking at up/down sloping MACD. Just because MACD is dynamic (combined with BB) doesn't do much good in this system the way it is used!. Also adding TM to the mix does little good as it is nothing much more than CCI (if you trade color only same as trading CCI).  
  
Before you comment this I suggest you do your homework first...  
Manual for BB-MACD use:  
[http://www.nexgent3.com/Nexgen%20Sof...ay1%202010.pdf](http://www.nexgent3.com/Nexgen%20Software%20Services%20User%20Guide%20May1%202010.pdf)  
  
Videos where BB-MACD used:  
[http://www.nexgent3.com/newvideos/Fi...pe%20Trade.htm](http://www.nexgent3.com/newvideos/Fibonacci%20Momentum%20Type%20Trade/Fibonacci%20Momentum%20Type%20Trade.htm)  
  
[http://www.nexgent3.com/newvideos/Fi...pe%20Trade.htm](http://www.nexgent3.com/newvideos/Fibonacci%20Momentum%20Type%20Trade/Fibonacci%20Momentum%20Type%20Trade.htm)  
  
ps.  
I'm currently programming Nexgen T3 indicators (of which BB-MACD is one) for MT4, I am also testing them on MT4 tick charts (build with custom script). I might even start a new tread about that here or TSD, but for now I prefer to stay private with it... ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) Anyone who can contribute is welcome to join and PM me...  
  
Here is a screen shot of the system on MT4 25 tick chart:

Hi Trend Magic Traders,  
  
  
I have a very similar method for Daily Charts and just wanted to get feedback on Trend Magic Entries . It seems that if we also added 1 more rule ( filter ) for entries it might help increase winning % and reduce drawdown on trades. Since we are entering " Long " above TM and " Short " below TM we are in affect using TM Indcator as Support and Resistance. One filter we might add to entries is " only take LONG entry if opening of entry bar opens above TM and only take SHORT entry if opening of entry bar opens below TM ? This way we are entering LONG trades above resistance (TM) and entering SHORT trades below resistance ( TM ).   
Any thoughts ?   
  
  
Thanks for sharing TM Method Paulus I have followed it since the original thread with Tudorgirl.  
  
EZ Trades

I'm new to FF and the original of this thread is the first one I've read. I'm just wondering if there are still interest in writing such a strategy into an EA? As someone who always use EAs, I can't imagine how can anyone validate a system without making it mechanical and test it over time. Visual testing is far far from accurate and forward testing is usually too slow to build enough data to draw concrete conclusions.  
  
TM is a good trend indicator however because of of repaint issues, I would choose to use TG's MTF indicator, which doesn't repaint. I know some people who had trouble using it, although in my view, if you use it correctly, it does have value.

  * [#395](/thread/post/4678636#post4678636 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 10, 2011 1:05am  Jun 10, 2011 1:05am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar160495_3.gif) minmin830](minmin830)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2010 | [82 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=160495)

How can any trend indicator with any kind of accuracy not being a lagging indicator? Can someone foresee the future? I don't think so.  
  
This is what we have to live with. If you want a indicator provide stable and accurate signals, it'll be lagging and not sensitive to price movement, as a result under the market condition when there's no sustained movement it'll likely only tell the trend near it's exhaustion point. However, during long movement, it keeps you in and capture more profits.  
  
On the other hand, if you have a indicator that is very sensitive to price movement and "foresee" the future price, you will get repaint problems as well as many fake signals during choppy markets. I don't care how mathematically advanced you are, you can't get around it. As no one can tell where the price is going to move in the further, all they can do is "repaint".  
  
I agree with the above, money management are key. So far the two most useful tools I find in trading are: well capitalized account that can sustain temporary set backs and sensible take profit. The deeper the pockets, the easier to make money. 

Wise-EA MT4 Programming

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#398](/thread/post/4684105#post4684105 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 12, 2011 8:19pm  Jun 12, 2011 8:19pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar105831_3.gif) Jani72](jani72)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [40 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=105831)

I'm not sure how the current TM works, but atleast the one i used a while ago had a redrawing issue.  
  
Problem with TM comes when CCI crosses 0-level and TM will redraw, so what you see on history chart is not what you see on live trading!   
  
I used TM (actually just CCI) in one EA and solved the redrawing by programming a parameter for treshold margin around 0-level, so inside this margin no buy/sell signals are given only on crossing treshold up or down and if treshold set to 0 indi works as original. For example if treshold set to 20 indi value neds to go above 20 or below -20 to give entry signal (TM to change color) in between we are in no action zone indicator drawing yellow

The name of the indicator is BB MACD cct.ex4, and you can download it from this thread - Post #2.  
  
Instead of 1 MACD BB indicator I actually use two instances of the same indicator. I call these the Fast and Slow MACDs. Here are the settings  
  
FAST MACD BB (38, 120, 20, 1.1)  
SLOW MACD BB (144, 233, 20, 1.1)

Hi
